They cut okay but definitely nowhere as close or powerful a shave as the T-Edger. These run quiet and smooth and cut so-so but don't quite get that skin close feel. The T-Edgers are louder, feel more powerful and seem to cut better. In fact, I switched from this brand new Outliner to the seven-year-old Edger it was supposed to replace during the very first cut. Even at seven-years old, the Edger still seemed to cut better. Maybe it's personal preference but if you're on the fence over the Outliner or Edger for facial shaving and head balding, I definitely give my nod to the Edger.<br /><br />My son and I cannot use conventional manual or disposable razors due to razor bumps. Electric razors, especially the rotary type like Norelco, are just as bad. When we want a skin-close shave without bumps or irritation, nothing beats a good set of Andis edgers or outliners. I bought this set for my son and they work great. He even uses them for shaving before his monthly Army drills, so that should tell you how close they shave. You will get a shave just as close as a blade without going under the skin and inducing the growth of bumps. That doesn't mean bumps aren't possible. You can still get bumps if you don't clean, sterilize and lube the blades after each use. This inhibits the growth of germs and bacteria and keeps the blades sharp and smooth so they don't develop microscopic pits that snag hairs and cause bumps and irritations. Also, remember to always shave with the grain. Shaving against it will produce bumps, even with clippers like these.ers like these.
